            <span>Download PDF</span>
            <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xlink:href="#global-icon-download"/></svg>
        </a>
    </div>
    

                        
                    </div>
                
                
                    <section aria-labelledby="Sec1" data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>Male–female gamete size dimorphism is a fundamental trait found in most multicellular organisms including plants, animals, fungi, brown algae, red algae, and green algae, and has been a major topic of biological sciences since Charles Darwin first wrote on the topic of sexual selection<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Darwin, C. R. The Descent of Man, and Selection in Relation to Sex 1st edn, Vol. 1 (John Murray, London, 1871)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d13857e634">1</a></sup>. However, such dimorphism is not found in many unicellular species which typically produce morphologically identical gametes—“isogametes”. Thus, male and female gametes differing in size—known as anisogamy—emerged independently from isogamous ancestors in various eukaryotic lineages<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Bell, G. The evolution of anisogamy. J. Theor. Biol. 73, 247–270 (1978)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d13857e638">2</a></sup>. In most lineages, emergence of anisogamy was so ancient that isogamous close relatives are long extinct, making it difficult to infer the genetic bases for steps in the transition from isogamy to anisogamy and oogamy. In contrast, the entire volvocine lineage began diverging from a single-celled, isogamous <i>Chlamydomonas</i>-like ancestor ~200 MYA to give rise to genera exhibiting a range of morphological and reproductive patterns including single-celled isogamous <i>Chlamydomonas</i>, 8- or 16-celled isogamous <i>Gonium</i>, 32-celled isogamous <i>Yamagishiella</i>, 32-celled anisogamous <i>Eudorina</i>, and &gt;500-celled oogamous <i>Volvox</i> (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">1</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Nozaki, H. Origin and evolution of the genera Pleodorina and Volvox (Volvocales). Biologia 58, 425–431 (2003)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d13857e664">3</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Herron, M. D., Hackett, J. D., Aylward, F. O. &amp; Michod, R. E. Triassic origin and early radiation of multicellular volvocine algae. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 106, 3254–3258 (2009)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d13857e667">4</a></sup>; thus providing a rich source of material for comparative evolutionary studies of sexual cycles. Furthermore, sex-determining genes and sex chromosomal regions or mating-type loci (<i>MT</i>) have been studied extensively in both isogamous and sexually dimorphic volvocine green algae<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ferris, P. J. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. The mating-type locus of Chlamydomonas reinhardtii contains highly rearranged DNA sequences. Cell 76, 1135–1145 (1994)." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d13857e675">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ferris, P. J. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. Mating type in Chlamydomonas is specified by mid, the minus-dominance gene. Genetics 146, 859–869 (1997)." href="#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d13857e675_1">6</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Nozaki, H., Mori, T., Misumi, O., Matsunaga, S. &amp; Kuroiwa, T. Males evolved from the dominant isogametic mating type. Curr. Biol. 16, R1018–R1020 (2006)." href="#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d13857e675_2">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Identification of the minus-dominance gene ortholog in the mating-type locus of Gonium pectorale. Genetics 178, 283–294 (2008)." href="#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d13857e675_3">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e675_4">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Geng, S., De Hoff, P. &amp; Umen, J. G. Evolution of sexes from an ancestral mating-type specification pathway. PLoS Biol. 12, e1001904 (2014)." href="#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d13857e675_5">10</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e678">11</a></sup>. Therefore, this green algal group represents a unique model lineage for investigating the transition from isogamy to anisogamy based on molecular genetic data.</p><p>Charlesworth<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Charlesworth, B. The population genetics of anisogamy. J. Theor. Biol. 73, 347–357 (1978)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d13857e685">12</a></sup> predicted that anisogamy could evolve from an isogamous genetic sex-determination system with two haploid mating types if an autosomally encoded gamete cell-size-determining gene with dimorphic alleles became loosely linked to the mating locus. Under conditions where anisogamy is favored, selection would act to promote closer linkage between the cell-size locus and mating locus, with an endpoint of complete linkage disequilibrium that might be achieved through suppression of recombination. A secondary outcome of generating a region of suppressed recombination near the mating locus would be potential for the <i>MT</i> region to capture additional genes through inversions or transposition, and to retain genes or alleles that are beneficial for their respective sex<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Bull, J. J. Sex chromosomes in haploid dioecy: a unique contrast to muller’s theory for diploid dioecy. Am. Nat. 112, 245–250 (1978)." href="#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d13857e692">13</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Bachtrog, D. et al. Are all sex chromosomes created equal? Trends Genet. 27, 350–357 (2011)." href="#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d13857e692_1">14</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Immler, S. &amp; Otto, S. P. The evolution of sex chromosomes in organisms with separate haploid sexes. Evolution 69, 694–708 (2015)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d13857e695">15</a></sup>. Thus, it is predicted that anisogamous or oogamous volvocine species will have relatively complex multi-genic <i>MT</i> loci compared with <i>MT</i> loci from isogamous species, and may contain additional genes that govern gamete size and/or other sexually selected traits. A previous comparative study of the <i>Volvox carteri</i> and <i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii MT</i> loci was consistent with the idea of massive expansion of the mating locus in <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> with incorporation of many new genes, including at least one dimorphic size control gene, <i>MAT3</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e720">9</a></sup>, a mammalian Retinoblastoma tumor suppressor (RB) homolog in the volvocine algae that regulates the cell cycle and maintains cell size in <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Umen, J. G. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. Control of cell division by a retinoblastoma protein homolog in Chlamydomonas. Genes Dev. 15, 1652–1661 (2001)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d13857e730">16</a></sup>. The <i>V</i>. <i>carteri MAT3</i> homolog resides within <i>MT</i> and shows extensive divergence between male and female haplotypes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e744">9</a></sup>. Although this <i>MAT3</i> allelic dimorphism was once hypothesized to be involved in establishing anisogamy<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e751">9</a></sup>, a subsequent comparative analysis of the <i>MAT3</i> sequences from various isogamous, anisogamous, and oogamous volvocine organisms indicated that the extensive <i>MAT3</i> divergence in the <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> lineage appear to have occurred subsequent to the emergence of anisogamy, and therefore, <i>MAT3</i> dimorphism may not be directly related to the origins of male–female gamete size dimorphism in volvocine algae<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Hiraide, R. et al. The evolution of male-female sexual dimorphism predates the gender-based divergence of the mating locus gene MAT3/RB. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 1038–1040 (2013)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d13857e771">17</a></sup>. While <i>MT</i> sequences of <i>Gonium pectorale</i>, an isogamous volvocine alga more closely related to oogamous <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> than to <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i>, has been also determined<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e794">11</a></sup>, the lack of information on <i>MT</i> structures at intermediate isogamous and anisogamous stages in volvocine evolution leaves open important questions about how changes in <i>MT</i> structure and gene content relate to transitions from isogamy to anisogamy. Although Geng et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Geng, S., De Hoff, P. &amp; Umen, J. G. Evolution of sexes from an ancestral mating-type specification pathway. PLoS Biol. 12, e1001904 (2014)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d13857e805">10</a></sup> showed that the <i>V</i>. <i>carteri MID</i> gene on its own can govern key aspects of gamete dimorphism, that study did not address the evolution of structural complexity in volvocine <i>MT</i>.</p><p>In this study, we focus on a more suitable combination for a comparative study of the transition from isogamy to anisogamy: two closely related intermediate volvocine species that bracket the transition from isogamy to anisogamy—isogamous <i>Yamagishiella unicocca</i> and anisogamous <i>Eudorina</i> sp., both of which share essentially the same vegetative (asexual) morphology (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig1">1</a>, Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">1</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Nozaki, H. Morphology and evolution of sexual reproduction in the Volvocaceae (Chlorophyta). J. Plant Res. 109, 353–361 (1996)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d13857e833">18</a></sup>. We sequence the whole nuclear genomes of both mating types or sexes of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and <i>Eudorina</i> sp., and identify and characterize their respective <i>MT</i> regions. Contrary to expectations for increased <i>MT</i> size and gene content evolving during the transition to anisogamy, the <i>Eudorina</i> sp. male and female <i>MT</i> haplotypes are very small, 7 kb and 90 kb in size, respectively, with only two sex-specific genes and two pairs of gametologs (i.e., genes with alleles in both mating haplotypes). The highly reduced <i>MT</i> structures of <i>Eudorina</i> sp. indicates that anisogamy can evolve from isogamy without the addition of a gamete-size-control gene and without increased <i>MT</i> size and complexity.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Fig. 1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs42003-018-0019-5/MediaObjects/42003_2018_19_Fig1_HTML.jpg?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-1-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs42003-018-0019-5/MediaObjects/42003_2018_19_Fig1_HTML.jpg" alt="figure1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="460" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p>Volvocine green algal phylogeny<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Nozaki, H. Origin and evolution of the genera Pleodorina and Volvox (Volvocales). Biologia 58, 425–431 (2003)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d13857e879">3</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Herron, M. D., Hackett, J. D., Aylward, F. O. &amp; Michod, R. E. Triassic origin and early radiation of multicellular volvocine algae. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 106, 3254–3258 (2009)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d13857e882">4</a></sup> and mating-type locus (<i>MT</i>) evolution. Phylogenetic relationships of volvocine algae are illustrated with vegetative morphology, gamete morphology<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Nozaki, H. Morphology and evolution of sexual reproduction in the Volvocaceae (Chlorophyta). J. Plant Res. 109, 353–361 (1996)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d13857e889">18</a></sup>, and <i>MT</i> structures of <i>Yamagishiella unicocca</i>, <i>Eudorina</i> sp., and three other species previously studied (<i>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="De Hoff, P. L. et al. Species and population level molecular profiling reveals cryptic recombination and emergent asymmetry in the dimorphic mating locus of C. reinhardtii. PLoS Genet. 9, e1003724 (2013)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d13857e905">25</a></sup>, <i>Gonium pectorale</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e911">11</a></sup>, and <i>Volvox carteri</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e917">9</a></sup>). The bars at the flagellar bases of the isogametes indicate tubular mating structures (TMS)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Nozaki, H. Morphology and evolution of sexual reproduction in the Volvocaceae (Chlorophyta). J. Plant Res. 109, 353–361 (1996)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d13857e922">18</a></sup>. In <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i>, only the <i>plus</i> gametes possess TMS (red bar). In <i>G</i>. <i>pectorale</i> and <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i>, both the <i>plus</i> and <i>minus</i> gametes possess TMS (red and blue bars, respectively)</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec2" data-title="Results"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2">Results</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3">Mating-type loci (<i>MT</i>) of <i>Yamagishiella</i> and <i>Eudorina</i>
                        </h3><p>We de novo sequenced whole genomes from both sexes of isogamous <i>Y. unicocca</i> and anisogamous <i>Eudorina</i> sp., and obtained resultant assemblies as follows: <i>plus</i> strain of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> (2012-1026-YU-F2-6/NIES-3982, assembly “YamagishiellaPlus_1.0”), total length 134,234,618 bp of 1461 contigs with N50 of 666,310 bp; <i>minus</i> strain of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> (2012-1026-YU-F2-1/NIES-3983, assembly “YamagishiellaMinus_1.0”), total length 140,837,241 bp of 1897 contigs with N50 of 547,037 bp; male strain of <i>Eudorina</i> sp. (2010-623-F1-E3/NIES-4100, assembly “EudorinaMale_1.0”), total length 168,620,790 bp of 2471 contigs with N50 of 377,357 bp; and female strain of <i>Eudorina</i> sp. (2010-623-F1-E8/NIES-4018, assembly “EudorinaFemale_1.0”), total length 184,032,255 bp of 3180 contigs with N50 of 564,035 bp. The resultant assemblies contained dimorphic (rearranged) haplotype regions that composed <i>MT</i> (Supplementary Figs <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">2</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">3</a>). <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca plus</i> and <i>minus MT</i> regions were 268 and 165 kb in size, respectively, which is somewhat smaller than the <i>MT</i> regions of <i>C. reinhardtii</i> and <i>G. pectorale</i> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig1">1</a>, Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">1</a>). <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca MT</i> included two inverted syntenic blocs of 9 and 7 collinear gametologs, and a single gene, <i>CRB1</i>, that was outside these two syntenic blocs (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig2">2a</a>). Two conserved sex-limited genes, <i>minus</i>-limited <i>MID</i> and <i>plus</i>-limited <i>FUS1</i> (Supplementary Figs <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">4</a>–<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">8</a>), were also present. <i>Eudorina</i> sp. female and male <i>MT</i> haplotypes were the most highly reduced of any volvocine algal species described to date, measuring 90 and 7 kb in size, respectively (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig2">2b</a>, Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">1</a>). Only two gametologs, <i>SPS1</i> (encoding a putative spermine syntase similar to ACAULIS5 required for stem elongation in flowering plants<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Hanzawa, Y. et al. ACAULIS5, an Arabidopsis gene required for stem elongation, encodes a spermine synthase. EMBO J. 19, 4248–4256 (2000)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1098">19</a></sup>) and <i>UNC50</i> (encoding a membrane trafficking protein homolog conserved in eukaryotes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Fang, Z., Zhou, L., Jiang, S., Cao, L. &amp; Yu, L. UNC50 prompts G1/S transition and proliferation in HCC by regulation of epidermal growth factor receptor trafficking. PLoS ONE 10, e0119338 (2015)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1105">20</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Selyunin, A. S., Iles, L. R., Bartholomeusz, G. &amp; Mukhopadhyay, S. Genome-wide siRNA screen identifies UNC50 as a regulator of Shiga toxin 2 trafficking. J. Cell Biol. 216, 3249–3262 (2017)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1108">21</a></sup>), were found in <i>Eudorina</i> sp. <i>MT</i> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig2">2b</a>). <i>MID</i> and <i>FUS1</i> homologs were also found in the male and female <i>MT</i>, respectively, as sex-limited genes. The size and GC contents of whole genome and <i>MT</i> of the two algae with the other volvocine species so far analyzed<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Ferris, P. J. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. The mating-type locus of Chlamydomonas reinhardtii contains highly rearranged DNA sequences. Cell 76, 1135–1145 (1994)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1134">5</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1137">9</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1140">11</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Ferris, P. J., Armbrust, E. V. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. Genetic structure of the mating-type locus of Chlamydomonas reinhardtii. Genetics 160, 181–200 (2002)." href="#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1143">22</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Merchant, S. S. et al. The Chlamydomonas genome reveals the evolution of key animal and plant functions. Science 318, 245–250 (2007)." href="#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1143_1">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Prochnik, S. E. et al. Genomic analysis of organismal complexity in the multicellular green alga Volvox carteri. Science 329, 223–226 (2010)." href="#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1143_2">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="De Hoff, P. L. et al. Species and population level molecular profiling reveals cryptic recombination and emergent asymmetry in the dimorphic mating locus of C. reinhardtii. PLoS Genet. 9, e1003724 (2013)." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1143_3">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Hanschen, E. R. et al. The Gonium pectorale genome demonstrates co-option of cell cycle regulation during the evolution of multicellularity. Nat. Commun. 7, 11370 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1146">26</a></sup> are summarized in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">1</a>.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Fig. 2"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 2</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5/figures/2" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs42003-018-0019-5/MediaObjects/42003_2018_19_Fig2_HTML.jpg?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-2-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs42003-018-0019-5/MediaObjects/42003_2018_19_Fig2_HTML.jpg" alt="figure2" loading="lazy" width="685" height="761" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-2-desc"><p><i>MT</i> structures and molecular evolutionary analyses of <i>MT</i> gametologs in isogamous <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and anisogamous <i>Eudorina</i> sp. <b>a, b</b> <i>MT</i> structures with sex-limited genes (<i>FUS1</i>, backed red; <i>MID</i>, blue) and gametologs of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> (<b>a</b>) and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. (<b>b</b>) (accession nos. LC314412–LC314415). Red regions represent <i>plus</i>/female <i>MT</i>. Blue regions represent <i>minus</i>/male <i>MT</i>. Gray shading indicate a syntenic bloc. Open triangles in <b>a</b> indicate gaps between scaffolds of the de novo whole genome assembly (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">2</a>). <b>c</b> Box-whisker plots comparing the distributions of synonymous (<i>d</i><sub>S</sub>, green/left) and non-synonymous (<i>d</i><sub>N</sub>, orange/right) substitution values for gametolog pairs found in rearranged regions of volvocine algal <i>MT</i> loci. Open dots are outliers from interquartile ranges except for those of <i>Eudorina</i> sp. which indicate two gametologs. <b>d</b>, <b>e</b> The <i>d</i><sub>N</sub>/<i>d</i><sub>S</sub> ratios of gametologs in rearranged (gray-shaded gene names) and flanking autosomal regions of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> (<b>d</b>) and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. (<b>e</b>) <i>MT</i>. There are no prominently dimorphic gametologs under positive selection between sexes/mating types (<i>d</i><sub>N</sub>/<i>d</i><sub>S</sub> &gt; 1)</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Another striking finding in this study was the highly dynamic nature of <i>MT</i> haplotype structure that shows no continuity among the five volvocine <i>MT</i> regions (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig1">1</a>; Supplementary Data <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM3">1</a>). Our data suggest relatively frequent turnover and haplotype reformation within <i>MT</i>, and explain the initially puzzling lack of continuity (e.g., evolutionary strata) observed between <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i> and <i>V. carteri MT</i> regions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1322">9</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Charlesworth, D. &amp; Charlesworth, B. Evolutionary biology: the origins of two sexes. Curr. Biol. 20, R519–R521 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1325">27</a></sup>. Distribution of homologs of <i>MT</i> and <i>MT</i>-linked genes in the five volvocine algae (Supplementary Data <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM3">1</a>) shows that most of these genes share the linkage to <i>MT</i>, except for <i>G</i>. <i>pectorale</i> in which majority of homologs of <i>MT</i> and <i>MT</i>-linked genes in other volvocine species are relocated to other genomic (autosomal) regions of <i>G</i>. <i>pectorale</i> as reported previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1361">11</a></sup>. Our data further suggest that the differences in size, gene content, and structure we have observed between volvocine <i>MT</i> loci are largely uncoupled from the transition to anisogamy in this lineage.</p><p>Gametolog divergence rates for <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. <i>MT</i> were compared to those of the other volvocine algae (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig2">2c, d, e</a>). Synonymous and non-synonymous substitutions (<i>d</i><sub>S</sub> and <i>d</i><sub>N</sub>) of gametologs between mating haplotypes in these two species were smaller than those of <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i>. Within the <i>Eudorina</i> sp. and <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> gametologs, <i>Eudorina</i> sp. <i>SPS1</i> and <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca CRB1</i> had relatively high <i>d</i><sub>S</sub> and <i>d</i><sub>N</sub> values (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig2">2d, e</a>). However, the <i>d</i><sub>N</sub>/<i>d</i><sub>S</sub> ratios of these two gametologs were low. Thus, we could not detect any strong patterns of selection or functional divergence between genes in the mating haplotypes of isogamous <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and anisogamous <i>Eudorina</i> sp.</p><p>Overall, <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. <i>MT</i> were smaller and simpler than <i>MT</i> regions from other volvocine species with only two conserved sex-limited genes (<i>MID</i> and <i>FUS1</i>) and no other clear examples of gametolog dimorphism. Some of the sex-limited gene homologs of oogamous <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> (<i>VcFSI1f, VcHMG1f</i>, and <i>VcMTM0097</i>) were conserved in the genomes of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and/or <i>Eudorina</i> sp. but they were autosomally encoded (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">2</a>). The <i>MTD1</i> gene is a <i>minus</i>-limited gene in <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i> and <i>G</i>. <i>pectorale</i>, while in <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. <i>MTD1</i> homologs are autosomal, but located nearby the <i>MT</i> region (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig1">1</a>, Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">2</a>). The presence of only two ancestral mating type genes (<i>MID</i> and <i>FUS1</i>) and lack of prominently divergent gametologs in highly reduced <i>Eudorina</i> sp. <i>MT</i> strongly disfavors the hypothesis that new sex-specific cell size-determining genes were acquired in <i>MT</i> during the emergence of anisogamy in the volvocine lineage<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Charlesworth, B. The population genetics of anisogamy. J. Theor. Biol. 73, 347–357 (1978)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1560">12</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Charlesworth, D. &amp; Charlesworth, B. Evolutionary biology: the origins of two sexes. Curr. Biol. 20, R519–R521 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1563">27</a></sup>.</p><p>Since female gametes of <i>Eudorina</i> and isogametes of <i>Yamagishiella</i> have no prominent morphological differentiation from their respective vegetative cells (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig3">3a, b</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Nozaki, H. Morphology and evolution of sexual reproduction in the Volvocaceae (Chlorophyta). J. Plant Res. 109, 353–361 (1996)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1580">18</a></sup>, the emergence of anisogamy from isogamy in the <i>Yamagishiella</i>/<i>Eudorina</i>-like ancestor appears to have been based on acquisition of the ability to form small male gametes. The present genome comparison demonstrated that the only male-limited gene in <i>Eudorina MT</i> is <i>MID</i> (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig2">2b</a>). The <i>MID</i> gene is present only in the <i>minus</i>/male <i>MT</i> haplotypes of heterothallic volvocine organisms<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Yamamoto, K. et al. Molecular evolutionary analysis of a gender-limited MID ortholog from the homothallic species Volvox africanus with male and monoecious spheroids. PLoS ONE 12, e0180313 (2017)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1610">28</a></sup> and serves as a master regulator for mating-type determination in isogamous <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Ferris, P. J. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. Mating type in Chlamydomonas is specified by mid, the minus-dominance gene. Genetics 146, 859–869 (1997)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1619">6</a></sup>. Recent molecular genetic approach in oogamous <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> showed that transformation of a female strain with <i>MID</i> enables the eggs (female gametes) to produce sperm packets (bundles of male gametes) and that a <i>MID</i>-knocked down male strain produces androgonidia (male reproductive initials) that can function as eggs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Geng, S., De Hoff, P. &amp; Umen, J. G. Evolution of sexes from an ancestral mating-type specification pathway. PLoS Biol. 12, e1001904 (2014)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1636">10</a></sup>. Therefore, although there are an additional eight male-limited and five female-limited <i>MT</i> genes in the expanded <i>MT</i> of <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1652">9</a></sup> that likely play a role in gamete fitness and early sexual development, none of them other than <i>MID</i> appear to have an essential role for the dimorphic gamete differentiation<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Geng, S., De Hoff, P. &amp; Umen, J. G. Evolution of sexes from an ancestral mating-type specification pathway. PLoS Biol. 12, e1001904 (2014)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1659">10</a></sup>. It follows that the evolution of males in volvocine algae might have resulted from altered function of the sex-determining protein MID or its target genes.</p><p>The isogamous FUS1 protein is a single-pass transmembrane protein that is present on the mating structure of <i>plus</i> gametes and required to recognize and adhere to <i>minus</i> gametes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1672">11</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Ferris, P. J., Woessner, J. P. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. A sex recognition glycoprotein is encoded by the plus mating-type gene fus1 of Chlamydomonas reinhardtii. Mol. Biol. Cell 7, 1235–1248 (1996)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1675">29</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Misamore, M. J., Gupta, S. &amp; Snell, W. J. The Chlamydomonas Fus1 protein is present on the mating type plus fusion organelle and required for a critical membrane adhesion event during fusion with minus gametes. Mol. Biol. Cell 14, 2530–2542 (2003)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1678">30</a></sup>. Previously, <i>FUS1</i> homologs have been reported in isogamous <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Ferris, P. J., Woessner, J. P. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. A sex recognition glycoprotein is encoded by the plus mating-type gene fus1 of Chlamydomonas reinhardtii. Mol. Biol. Cell 7, 1235–1248 (1996)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1691">29</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Misamore, M. J., Gupta, S. &amp; Snell, W. J. The Chlamydomonas Fus1 protein is present on the mating type plus fusion organelle and required for a critical membrane adhesion event during fusion with minus gametes. Mol. Biol. Cell 14, 2530–2542 (2003)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1694">30</a></sup> and <i>G</i>. <i>pectorale</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1703">11</a></sup>, but were not found in the oogamous <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> genome<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1714">9</a></sup>, suggesting that <i>FUS1</i> was lost at some point after the <i>G</i>. <i>pectorale–V. carteri</i> lineages split<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Mori, T., Kawai-Toyooka, H., Igawa, T. &amp; Nozaki, H. Gamete dialogs in green lineages. Mol. Plant 8, 1442–1454 (2015)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1727">31</a></sup>. Our data showed that isogamous <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and anisogamous <i>Eudorina</i> sp. both had a <i>FUS1</i> homolog that was <i>plus</i>- or female-limited in <i>MT</i>, respectively (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig2">2a, b</a>; Supplementary Figs <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">4</a>–<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">8</a>; Supplementary Note <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">1</a>), and suggest that loss of <i>FUS1</i> occurred subsequent to the <i>Eudorina</i>–<i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> split.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">Sex-related gene expressions in <i>Yamagishiella</i> and <i>Eudorina</i>
                        </h3><p>Expression programs of sex-related <i>MT</i> genes were evaluated for <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig3">3</a>). Unlike the case in <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i> and <i>G</i>. <i>pectorale</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Ferris, P. J. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. Mating type in Chlamydomonas is specified by mid, the minus-dominance gene. Genetics 146, 859–869 (1997)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1818">6</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Identification of the minus-dominance gene ortholog in the mating-type locus of Gonium pectorale. Genetics 178, 283–294 (2008)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1821">8</a></sup>, but similar to <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1831">9</a></sup>, the <i>MID</i> mRNA was expressed constitutively in <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca minus</i> cells and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. males. The gamete adhesion gene <i>FUS1</i> from <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca plus</i> was expressed only in gametes as is also the case for <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i> and <i>G</i>. <i>pectorale FUS1</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1869">11</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Ferris, P. J., Woessner, J. P. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. A sex recognition glycoprotein is encoded by the plus mating-type gene fus1 of Chlamydomonas reinhardtii. Mol. Biol. Cell 7, 1235–1248 (1996)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1872">29</a></sup>, but <i>Eudorina</i> sp. female <i>FUS1</i> was most strongly expressed after mixing female with male gametes. The <i>MTD1</i> gene in <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i> is found only in the <i>minus MT</i> haplotype, is expressed in gametes, and is required for efficient gametogenesis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Lin, H. &amp; Goodenough, U. W. Gametogenesis in the Chlamydomonas reinhardtii minus mating type is controlled by two genes, MID and MTD1. Genetics 176, 913–925 (2007)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1895">32</a></sup>, but appears to have lost its function in <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> where it is a pseudogene<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Ferris, P. et al. Evolution of an expanded sex-determining locus in Volvox. Science 328, 351–354 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d13857e1905">9</a></sup>. In <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and <i>Eudorina</i> sp., <i>MTD1</i> is autosomal with a copy in both sexes (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig1">1</a>, Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">2</a>). However, <i>MTD1</i> expression in both <i>Eudorina</i> sp. and <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> was restricted to <i>minus</i>/male gametes (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig3">3c, d</a>), indicating a conserved function in gametogenesis in all genera except <i>Volvox</i> (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">9</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">10</a>). The evolution of a highly reduced male <i>MT</i> in <i>Eudorina</i> sp. containing only the single male-limited <i>MID</i> gene might have been possible with minor changes that placed expression of <i>MTD1</i> under mating-type control allowing it to reside outside of the <i>MT</i> locus.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Fig. 3"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 3</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5/figures/3" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs42003-018-0019-5/MediaObjects/42003_2018_19_Fig3_HTML.jpg?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-3-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs42003-018-0019-5/MediaObjects/42003_2018_19_Fig3_HTML.jpg" alt="figure3" loading="lazy" width="685" height="495" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p>Sex induction and associated gene expression alternations in isogamous <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and anisogamous <i>Eudorina</i> sp. <b>a</b>, <b>b</b> Asexual and sex-induced individuals of opposite sexes of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> (<i>plus/minus</i>) (<b>a</b>) and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. (female/male) (<b>b</b>). Mating reactions (mixed, right panels) occurred after mixing induced cultures of the two sexes (middle panels). In <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> (<b>a</b>), clumping of the colonies and release of single-celled isogametes (arrowheads) were observed 1 h after mixing. In <i>Eudorina</i> sp. (<b>b</b>), sex induction treatment resulted in the formation of sperm packets and the packet dissociated into individual sperm that penetrated into a female colony (arrowheads) within 16 h after mixing. Scale bars, 20 µm. <b>c</b>, <b>d</b> Gene expression pattern of volvocine sex-limited genes in <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> (<b>c</b>) and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. (<b>d</b>). Semi-quantitative RT-PCR analyses were performed using the same cultures for <b>a</b> and <b>b</b>. All gels were run under the same experimental conditions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Kawai-Toyooka, H. et al. Sex-specific posttranslational regulation of the gamete fusogen GCS1 in the isogamous volvocine alga Gonium pectorale. Eukaryot. Cell 13, 648–656 (2014)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2062">44</a></sup>, and the cropped gel images are shown. Full-length gel images with size markers are presented in Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">11</a></p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5/figures/3" data-track-dest="link:Figure3 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec5" data-title="Conclusions"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec5-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec5">Conclusions</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec5-content"><p>We have illuminated here the initial transition of the sex-determining chromosomal region or <i>MT</i> during the evolution of anisogamy, and shown that anisogamy can evolve without increased <i>MT</i> complexity. Only two sex-limited genes that encode the sex-determining factor <i>MID</i> (<i>minus</i>/male) and the gamete recognition factor <i>FUS1</i> (<i>plus</i>/female) constitute the core of the <i>MT</i> haplotypes in both isogamous and anisogamous volvocine algae. Therefore, in this lineage the transition to anisogamy likely involved direct modification of the sex determination pathway controlled by <i>MID</i> rather than by acquisition of new gamete size control genes in <i>MT</i>. The presence of <i>FUS1</i> not only in isogamous but also in anisogamous volvocine algae suggests that both systems share the FUS1-dependent gamete recognition mechanism. Future investigation of sex-related genes and their roles in anisogamy and gamete dialogues in volvocine algae holds great promise for understanding the dynamics of mating system evolution in eukaryotes.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec6" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec6-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec6">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec6-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">Strains</h3><p>For <i>Yamagishiella</i>, <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> strains 2012-1026-YU-F2-6 (NIES-3982, mating-type <i>plus</i>) and 2012-1026-YU-F2-1 (NIES-3983, mating-type <i>minus</i>) were used throughout the study. For the whole-genome sequencing of <i>Eudorina</i>, <i>Eudorina</i> sp. strains 2010-623-F1-E4 (NIES-3984, female) and 2010-623-F1-E2 (NIES-3985, male) were used. In other <i>Eudorina</i> experiments, two other sibling strains of the former two, <i>Eudorina</i> sp. strains 2010-623-F1-E8 (NIES-4018, female) and 2010-623-F1-E3 (NIES-4100, male), were used unless otherwise stated.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec8">De novo whole genome assembly</h3><p>Genomic DNAs were prepared according to the method of Miller et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Miller, S. M., Schmitt, R. &amp; Kirk, D. L. Jordan, an active Volvox transposable element similar to higher plant transposons. Plant Cell 5, 1125–1138 (1993)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2164">33</a></sup>. Whole-genome sequencing of <i>plus</i> and <i>minus</i> strains of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and male and female strains of <i>Eudorina</i> sp. were performed using PacBio and Illumina technologies as described previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Multiple independent changes in mitochondrial genome conformation in chlamydomonadalean algae. Genome Biol. Evol. 9, 993–999, &#xA;                    https://doi.org/10.1093/gbe/evx060&#xA;                    &#xA;                   (2017)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2184">34</a></sup>. Briefly, genomic DNA was sheared using a DNA shearing tube, g-TUBE (Covaris). Several 20 kb libraries for P5-C3 and P6-C4 sequencing were constructed and sequenced on SMRT cells in PacBio RS II (Pacific Biosciences). These reactions generated 2.5 M and 4.1 M sub reads (total bases: 17.2 Gb and 22.8 Gb, respectively) for <i>plus</i> and <i>minus</i> strains of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i>, respectively, and 2.6 M and 4.4 M sub reads (total bases: 15.6 Gb and 23.0 Gb, respectively) for male and female strains of <i>Eudorina</i> sp., respectively. Sequencing coverage was about 128x, 162x, 93x, and 125x based on the estimated genome size, respectively. In each of the four strains, PacBio reads were assembled de novo with HGAP3 assembler (Pacific Biosciences). Furthermore, genomic DNA was fragmented using a DNA Shearing System, S2 Focused-ultrasonicator (Covaris). Illumina paired-end libraries (insert sizes with 400 bp for <i>plus</i> and <i>minus</i> strains of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i>, 600 bp for male strain of <i>Eudorina</i> sp., and 400 bp for female strain of <i>Eudorina</i> sp.) were constructed using a TruSeq DNA Sample Prep Kit (Illumina) according to the manufacturer instructions. These libraries were sequenced using Illumina HiSeq 2000 and 2500 sequencers (230.5 M and 197.0 M reads with 150 bp read length for <i>plus</i> and <i>minus</i> strains of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i>, respectively, 251.2 M reads with 250 bp read length for male strain of <i>Eudorina</i> sp., and 165.3 M reads with 100 bp read length for female strain of <i>Eudorina</i> sp.). Total bases and sequencing coverage were 34.6 Gb (258x), 29.5 Gb (210x), 62.8 Gb (372x), and 16.5 Gb (89x), respectively. The Illumina data were then mapped against the PacBio assembly sequence using BWA-MEM Release 0.7.7<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate long-read alignment with Burrows–Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 26, 589–595 (2010)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2242">35</a></sup> including error correction with the samtools/bcftools/vcfutils.pl program v0.1.19 (<a href="https://samtools.sourceforge.net/">https://samtools.sourceforge.net/</a>), ultimately giving a set of nuclear genome sequence. We performed a long-range scaffolding using paired-end Sanger sequences from 38,400 and 3840 fosmid clones of female and male strains of <i>Eudorina</i> sp., respectively (DRA: DRA004920, DRA002727, and DRA004919; whole genome assembly: BDSI01000001-BDSI01003180, BDSJ01000001-BDSJ01002471, BDSK01000001-BDSK01001897, BDSL01000001-BDSL01001461).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec9">Sex-determining region identification</h3><p>Candidate scaffolds for entire sex-determining regions (<i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca plus</i>: Scaffold0026/0199/0237; <i>minus</i>: Scaffold0005/0230/0253/0437/1431; <i>Eudorina</i> sp. Female: scaffold1024; male: scaffold1040) were screened as major significant matching subjects with more than three non-overlapping protein hits (cutoff maximum E-value: 1e−10<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Altschul, S. F., Gish, W., Miller, W., Myers, E. W. &amp; Lipman, D. J. Basic local alignment search tool. J. Mol. Biol. 215, 403–410 (1990)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2276">36</a></sup>) by TBLASTN (NCBI) on de novo assemblies of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. with 80 proteins on <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> female <i>MT</i> (Genbank Acc. No. GU784915) as queries and then dotplot-analyzed between haplotypes of same species using YASS (<a href="https://bioinfo.lifl.fr/yass/index.php">https://bioinfo.lifl.fr/yass/index.php</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Noe, L. &amp; Kucherov, G. YASS: enhancing the sensitivity of DNA similarity search. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, W540–W543 (2005)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2307">37</a></sup> to detect the rearranged genomic regions of <i>MT</i>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec10">Gene identification</h3><p>We performed TBLASTN searches against the genome assembly databases of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. with the volvocine sex-limited proteins (<i>Gonium pectorale</i> FUS1, BAU61607<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2334">11</a></sup>; <i>G</i>. <i>pectorale</i> MTD1, BAI49487<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Hamaji, T., Ferris, P. J., Nishii, I. &amp; Nozaki, H. Identification of the minus mating-type specific gene MTD1 from Gonium pectorale (Volvocales, Chlorophyta). J. Phycol. 45, 1310–1314 (2009)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2345">38</a></sup>) as the queries, retrieved sequences with the highest similarity, and designed gene-specific primers (listed in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">3</a>) based on these sequences. To identify the ORF sequences, polyadenylated mRNAs from each sample were isolated using Dynabeads Oligo (dT)<sub>25</sub> (Thermo Fisher Scientific), reverse transcribed with Superscript III reverse transcriptase (Thermo Fisher Scientific), and amplified with KOD FX Neo DNA polymerase (Toyobo) and the gene-specific primers. To obtain the full-length cDNA sequences, 5′RACE and 3′RACE were performed using the GeneRacer kit (Thermo Fisher Scientific). The PCR products were directly sequenced, or first cloned into the pCR4Blunt-TOPO vector (Thermo Fisher Scientific) and then sequenced, using an ABI PRISM 3100 Genetic Analyzer (Thermo Fisher Scientific) with a BigDye Terminator cycle sequencing ready reaction kit, v.3.1 (Thermo Fisher Scientific). Full-length <i>MID</i> genes of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> (<i>minus</i> strain NIES-1859) and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. (male strain NIES-2735) were determined using the degenerate PCR method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Nozaki, H., Mori, T., Misumi, O., Matsunaga, S. &amp; Kuroiwa, T. Males evolved from the dominant isogametic mating type. Curr. Biol. 16, R1018–R1020 (2006)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2370">7</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Identification of the minus-dominance gene ortholog in the mating-type locus of Gonium pectorale. Genetics 178, 283–294 (2008)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2373">8</a></sup>.</p><p>Other gene models on <i>MT</i> scaffolds were predicted by Augustus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Hoff, K. J. &amp; Stanke, M. WebAUGUSTUS—a web service for training AUGUSTUS and predicting genes in eukaryotes. Nucleic Acids Res. 41, W123–W128 (2013)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2383">39</a></sup> with the <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i> parameter and then manually curated based on the similarity among <i>C</i>. <i>reinhardtii</i> and <i>V</i>. <i>carteri</i> gene models (JGI).</p><p><i>MT</i> genome sequences harboring rearranged domains with sex-limited genes and gametologs in <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> and <i>Eudorina</i> sp. and the autosomal gene <i>YuMTD1</i> are available under accession numbers LC314412–LC314416.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec11">Preparation of asexual and sex-induced samples of <i>Yamagishiella</i> and <i>Eudorina</i>
                        </h3><p>Asexual samples of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> were obtained by culturing the algae in screw-cap tubes (18 × 150 mm) containing ~11 ml AF-6 medium<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Kato, S. Laboratory culture and morphology of Colacium vesiculosum Ehrb. (Euglenophyceae). Jpn. J. Phycol. 30, 63–67 (1982)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2445">40</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Kasai, F. et al. NIES-collection list of strains, 8th edition. Jpn. J. Phycol. 57, 1–350 (2009)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2448">41</a></sup>, on a 14-h light/10-h dark cycle (light intensity: 60–110 μmol m<sup>−2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>) at 23 °C for 3–5 days. To induce sexual reproduction of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i>, asexually growing algae (~0.2 ml) were inoculated into 11 ml “VTAC + soil extract medium” (VTAC medium<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Kasai, F. et al. NIES-collection list of strains, 8th edition. Jpn. J. Phycol. 57, 1–350 (2009)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2463">41</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Nozaki, H., Kuroiwa, H., Mita, T. &amp; Kuroiwa, T. Pleodorina japonica sp. nov. (Volvocales, Chlorophyta) with bacteria-like endosymbionts. Phycologia 28, 252–267 (1989)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2466">42</a></sup> supplemented with 3%(v/v) soil extract (~0.5 mg of paddy soil suspended in 20 ml distilled water and autoclaved for 10 min)) in a tube, and cultured for 8 days under the same condition. The algal culture of each sex was then transferred into Petri dishes (60 mm × 15 mm), incubated for further 4 days, and used as a sex-induced <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> sample for the following analysis. “Mixed” sample of <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> were obtained by mixing the sex-induced samples (1 ml each) of both mating types in Petri dishes (30 mm × 10 mm), which were subsequently incubated for 3 h under the same condition, and used for semiquantitative RT-PCR.</p><p>Asexual samples of <i>Eudorina</i> sp. were obtained by culturing the algae in the screw-cap tubes containing ~10 ml SVM medium<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Kirk, D. L. &amp; Kirk, M. M. Protein synthetic patterns during the asexual life cycle of Volvox carteri. Dev. Biol. 96, 493–506 (1983)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2489">43</a></sup>, on a 14-h light/10-h dark cycle (light intensity: 180–320 μmol m<sup>−2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>) at 25 °C for 3 days. To induce sexual reproduction of <i>Eudorina</i> sp., ~0.4 mL of asexually grown algae in SVM medium were inoculated into Petri dishes (60 mm × 15 mm) containing ~11 ml “VTAC + soil extract medium” and cultured for 3 days under the same condition. The 11 ml culture of each sex was then transferred into Petri dishes (90 mm × 20 mm), diluted with twice volume of mating medium<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Nozaki, H., Kuroiwa, H., Mita, T. &amp; Kuroiwa, T. Pleodorina japonica sp. nov. (Volvocales, Chlorophyta) with bacteria-like endosymbionts. Phycologia 28, 252–267 (1989)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2501">42</a></sup>, and cultured for further 8 h under the same condition to form a sex-induced male or female culture of <i>Eudorina</i> sp., in which formation of sperm packets was observed in the male strain (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#Fig3">3b</a>). “Mixed” samples of <i>Eudorina</i> sp. were prepared by mixing the sex-induced female and male samples (5 ml each) in Petri dishes (60 mm × 15 mm), subsequently incubated for 16 h under the same condition, and used for the following analysis.</p><p>All microscopic images were acquired using a BX53 microscope (Olympus) equipped with differential interference contrast optics. The digital images were captured using a DP71 camera (Olympus) with DP controller software (Olympus), and their levels were adjusted with Adobe Photoshop CS6 (Adobe Systems Inc.).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec12">Semiquantitative RT-PCR analysis</h3><p>From <i>Y</i>. <i>unicocca</i> samples, polyadenylated mRNAs were isolated using Dynabeads Oligo (dT)<sub>25</sub> and reverse transcribed as described above. From <i>Eudorina</i> samples, total RNAs were extracted with TRI reagent (Molecular Research Center), treated with DNase I (amplification grade; Thermo Fisher Scientific), and reverse transcribed with Superscript III reverse transcriptase and Oligo (dT)<sub>20</sub> primer (Thermo Fisher Scientific). PCR reactions were performed with KOD FX Neo DNA polymerase (Toyobo). Primer sequences and PCR condition are listed in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#MOESM1">3</a> online. Under the conditions, all primer sets produced amplicons of the expected size and sequence (confirmed by direct sequencing). The PCR products were electrophoresed on 2% (w/v) agarose gels and stained with ethidium bromide<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Kawai-Toyooka, H. et al. Sex-specific posttranslational regulation of the gamete fusogen GCS1 in the isogamous volvocine alga Gonium pectorale. Eukaryot. Cell 13, 648–656 (2014)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2542">44</a></sup>. The gel images were captured using a ChemiDoc XRS system (Bio-Rad) with Quantity One software (Bio-Rad) and their levels were adjusted as described above.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec13">Molecular evolutionary analysis</h3><p>Divergence scores of synonymous and non-synonymous substitutions between gametologs were computed using yn00 of the PAML4 package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586–1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2554">45</a></sup>; nonsynonymous and synonymous site divergence of aligned coding sequences of gametologs was calculated based on Yang and Nielsen<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Yang, Z. &amp; Nielsen, R. Estimating synonymous and nonsynonymous substitution rates under realistic evolutionary models. Mol. Biol. Evol. 17, 32–43 (2000)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2558">46</a></sup> with equal weighting between pathways, and the same codon frequency for all pairs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Hamaji, T. et al. Sequence of the Gonium pectorale mating locus reveals a complex and dynamic history of changes in volvocine algal mating haplotypes. G3 (Bethesda) 6, 1179–1189 (2016)." href="/articles/s42003-018-0019-5#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d13857e2562">11</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Data availability</h3><p>Raw reads, genome assemblies, and annotations were deposited at DDBJ/EMBL/GenBank under the accessions as follows; DRA: DRA004920, DRA002727, and DRA004919; whole genome assembly: BDSI01000001-BDSI01003180, BDSJ01000001-BDSJ01002471, BDSK01000001-BDSK01001897, BDSL01000001-BDSL01001461; annotations: LC314412- LC314416. All the other data generated or analyzed during this study are included in this published article and its Supplementary information.</p></div></div></section>

                <i>EvoDevo</i>
                (2020)
              </p>
            </li>
          
            <li class="c-article-further-reading__item js-ref-item" id="further-reading-item-4">
              <h3 class="c-article-further-reading__title">

                   data-track="click"
                   data-track-action="view further reading article"

                   id="title-link-4">

              </h3>

                  <li><span
                        class="js-separator"></span><span>Kazuto Yoshida</span></li><li><span
